< Text>
I've only gone to this gym a handful of times but so far so good! The membership set up was a little sketchy, but that could be because I'm used to going to bigger and corporately owned gyms. It was a little annoying to obtain my key but they really worked with me the best they could. The initial set up is also not done the way the agreement says it'll be done, but I'm assuming COVID has forced some changes to be made. I love that it's 24/7. It's the main reason I joined because it really works with my schedule. My only complaints so far is I think cleanings should be performed more often than they are currently. Not entirely because of the pandemic but because the bathroom (women's bathroom, in this case) has not been cleaned in a week and it's absolutely disgusting and no paper towels to dry your hands. I also wish there was a bit more floor space for floor exercises but I totally understand since the place is already pretty small as it is. I'd give this place 5 stars if it weren't for how disheveled and dirty it is. I wish there were half stars because I would technically give it a 4.5. The actual equipment needs to be bit tidied up as well. I do what I can on my part to keep it organized and clean. The actual equipment itself is pretty clean and everything I've used so far works!<//Text>

<Review>I‚Äôve known about All City Fitness since the guy first opened his doors a couple of years ago.  I‚Äôd been going to the Fit Republic nearby for several months already.  Now, I‚Äôm gonna admit that I was a little harsh with my appraisal of his gym at first glance.  See, as an avid and happy member of Fit Republic, I didn‚Äôt really think much of this gym.

Fast forward to now, Fit Republic (as well a host of other gyms) all have fallen prey to the pandemic, having had to close their doors.  This guy, however, still strong and, get this, actually growing.  It takes serious amount of business savvy to not just survive a financial situation that forces other gyms out of business but see growth like All City has.
With Fit Republic gone, I had to find myself a new gym to work out in.  I found myself at All City and have been here for a week.  Here‚Äôs how that week went:

Signing up was really easy.  Just hit their website, selected a membership package, paid and got all the necessary paperwork in my email within minutes.  The next day, I took that paperwork to the gym and promptly received my key fob.

Sunday was Pull Day for me.  The cables might seem humble, but they hit in all the right spots.  The weight plate numbering system on this cable machine is a bit odd, going 1,2,3,4,ect instead of lbs or kgs.  So, it takes a little feeling around for what weight is right for your goals.

Monday was Cardio/Core.  This gym has an Assault Bike.  I‚Äôd often heard of these from the Crossfit community and have always wanted to try one out.  Few gyms have these, and I was excited to see one here.  They are NO JOKE!

Tuesday was Leg Day.  I had to adjust my leg program to accommodate the smaller size of this gym.  Walking lunges just aren‚Äôt feasible here.  So, you‚Äôll have to work on regular lunges or split squats.  He has one squat rack here. At first glance, it looked like two, but it‚Äôs really just one and a pole to TRX gear.  It‚Äôs fine, I was able to get some squats in on this rack with little issue.  I appreciate how other member use the squat rack for squats and not for curls or other stuff they can do elsewhere.

Wednesday was Upper Body day, and I got a good feel for All City‚Äôs benches and dumbbells.  He‚Äôs got a good selection of dumbbells, going all the way to 100lbs.   The benches are decent, albeit showing some milage.

Friday was Leg Day again and this time I tried out the quasi-smith machine he has there.  It‚Äôs not a Smith Machine per se as, while it is on a rail, the bar can float freely to and fro, so there‚Äôs a stability element to be needed with this.  Plenty of plates to get some good numbers with on squats and deadlifts and I really do like the bumper plates he has.  The hex bar is also a welcome sight.

Saturday was Push Day.  He‚Äôs got this pec deck that is flat out amazing!  I‚Äôve never had a stronger connection on a pec deck before this one.  I‚Äôve had some truly great chest push days in my lifting lifetime, this will be counted as one of my best!

So, one week down and yeah, this gym can be a bit cramped and you‚Äôll want to plan around the gear he has.  But, he‚Äôs growing, I‚Äôm told there‚Äôs some squat cages and a hack squat coming in.  Then, there‚Äôs the new location in the strip mall near MacArthur that‚Äôs gonna open up soon, which is very big and spacious.  All in all, this gym really is great and a very, very good value for what you pay a month for it.

I highly recommend.<//Review><pictures>None</pictures>< UserId.>

I appreciated them calling so I could end my trip a little early instead of leaving her miserable. <Review>Been a donor for almost 2 years now. Every person on the staff here at Santa fe springs are always courteous, considerate and professional. I have never experienced any rudeness, arrogance or lack of empathy from any of the personalities here, and this is the only location I have donate at. Consistency is very important in life, and Consistency of Character is a quality which I take pleasure in whenever I encounter it, wherever I am. I have nothing bad to say about any of the staff, and I have found the routine here to be very efficient.

I have but one thing to mention which is the only thing that ever frustrates me from time to time.
Some times when there is a delay in the samples that are taken from each donation for screening, I find it a bit inconsiderate to me and my time that no one alerts me that there is a problem, like that or any other problem that might cause me to not be able to donate when I come in. I take public transportation to this office and when I go through everything I have to in order to make it here, I find it quite irritating to learn that there is an issue on your end which effects me on my end.
I dont like wasting my time, and I understand that things happen. But that is no excuse for inconsideration. I feel that a courtesy call should be made to those who might be effected by these kinds of hold ups. Waiting to tell us once we're already here and then turning us away is unacceptable. A simple call would save us a whole lot of time and travel money and frustration.

Aside from that, bravo.

Thank you for your time.

<time>1549050744580< /time><rating>3<//rating>< text>
For the most part, it's a decent place to donate at.  The staff is mostly friendly and will have a conversation with you as you donate as long as things are slow and there is no chaos.  However with that said (well typed) there are glitches and issues I have seen.
1. They would like you to donate on the same days over and over.  If you donate Tuesday and Thursday.  They want you to donate Tuesdays and Thursdays.  I get it, but let's see the problem with that, life happens and holidays happen.  So if you donate Tuesday and you have to work Thursday, or it's a holiday, your arm is sore and you just want to rest your arm one more  day or you have a family emergency and you can donate again on Friday.  You can't donate Tuesday you have to donate Wednesday.  When you try to explain the problem to an employee, they just hide behind rules and regulations and walk away without really explaining anything or asking if you would like to speak with a supervisor for a better explanation.
2.  I enjoy getting to know the employees and talking with them.  However, when you're hooked up to a machine and you hear an employee that is standing next to you start making comments "Men, who needs them.  We've got this".  Funny part is once my machine started glitching, she called a man to fix the problem. I think that the employees need to watch what is being said around your clients, you never know who is listening.
3. The kiosks have a few glitches and do not like to work properly.<//text>
